### BUG: `clearPoll` dependency in `useEffect`  
**Severity**: medium  
**Location**: `BuildAction`  
**Problem**: The `useEffect` hook for cleanup has `clearPoll` in its dependency array. While `clearPoll` is wrapped in `useCallback`, `useCallback` itself can return a new function instance if its dependencies change. In this specific case, `clearPoll` has no dependencies, so it will always be stable. However, if `clearPoll` were to ever have dependencies, listing it in `useEffect`'s dependency array could lead to the cleanup function being re-registered unnecessarily, or worse, if `clearPoll` itself was not properly memoized, it could lead to an infinite loop or unexpected behavior. The comment states "listing it in the dependency array keeps the linter and React happy and ensures the cleanup always uses the canonical clearPoll logic," which is a misunderstanding of `useEffect` dependencies. For cleanup functions, if the cleanup logic itself doesn't depend on props or state that change during the component's lifecycle, it's often better to omit it from the dependency array or ensure it's truly stable. In this case, `clearPoll` is stable, s

### BUG: Incorrect `portable_sed` usage in `act4_start_and_register` for `MAILMAN-CLAUDE.md`  
**Severity**: high  
**Location**: `act4_start_and_register`  
**Problem**: When creating the `MAILMAN-CLAUDE.md` file for the mailman agent, the `portable_sed` command is used to substitute `{{ACTIVE_GATEWAYS_LIST}}`. The `gw_list` variable, which contains the formatted list of gateways, is passed directly to `portable_sed`. If `gw_list` contains characters that are special to `sed` (like `&`, `/`, `\`, `[`, `*`, etc.), `sed` will interpret them as part of the regular expression or replacement string, leading to incorrect substitutions or `sed` errors. This is especially problematic because `gw_list` is constructed with newlines (`\n`), which `sed` might misinterpret depending on the `sed` version and flags. The `safe_dir` variable is correctly escaped for `sed` metacharacters, but `gw_list` is not.  
**Fix**: The `gw_list` variable needs to be escaped before being passed to `portable_sed` to ensure that any special characters it might contain are treated as literal strings. This can be done by using a similar escaping mechanism as `safe_dir`.

### BUG: Incorrect `getSkillKey` for 'repo' type  
**Severity**: high  
**Location**: `getSkillKey`  
**Problem**: The `getSkillKey` function for `repo` type skills uses `skill.url` and `skill.skillPath`. However, the `PluginSkillSelection` type for `repo` skills (as implied by `RepoScanner` and its `onAddSkill` prop) should include `repoId` and `skillId` to uniquely identify a skill within a scanned repository. Using `url` and `skillPath` might not be unique enough if multiple skills from the same path but different repos (or different versions of the same repo) are considered, or if the `skillPath` itself isn't unique across different skills within the same repo. More critically, the `RepoScanner` component's `onAddSkill` prop expects a `PluginSkillSelection` which, for `repo` type, should contain `repoId` and `skillId`. The current implementation of `getSkillKey` does not align with the expected structure of a `repo` skill as it would be added by `RepoScanner`.

**Problem**: The `scanRepo` function is called with `body.ref || 'main'`. This means if `body.ref` is an empty string (`''`), it will default to `'main'`. However, an empty string for `ref` might be a valid, albeit unusual, input that should be passed to `scanRepo` if the intention is to allow an empty string as a reference. ### BUG: Race condition in activeOps counter  
**Severity**: high  
**Location**: `buildPlugin`, `scanRepo`, `pushToGitHub`  
**Problem**: The `activeOps` counter is incremented at the beginning of the `try` block and decremented in the `finally` block. However, if an asynchronous operation within the `try` block (e.g., `await runBuild(...)` in `buildPlugin`, `await execPromise(...)` in `scanRepo` or `pushToGitHub`) throws an error *before* the `await` keyword, the `finally` block will be executed immediately, decrementing `activeOps`. If the `await`ed promise then also rejects, the `finally` block will be executed *again* when the outer `catch` block finishes, leading to `activeOps` being decremented twice for a single operation. This can cause `activeOps` to become negative or incorrectly low, allowing more concurrent operations than `MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS`.  
**Fix**: The `activeOps` counter should be incremented *after* the concurrency check and *before* any asynchronous operations that could lead to an early `finally` execution. A more robust approach is to use a semaphore or a dedicated queue for managing concurrency, but a simpler fix for this pattern is to ensure the increment happens just before the main work starts and the decrement is guaranteed to happen only once per logical operation. For `buildPlugin`, `scanRepo`, and `pushToGitHub`, the increment should happen *after* initial synchronous validations and *before* the first `await` that performs the core work.  

For `buildPlugin`:  
```typescript
  // Concurrency guard
  if (activeOps >= MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS) {
    return { error: 'Too many concurrent builds. Please wait and try again.', status: 429 }
  }

  // Increment before the try block so the finally always decrements exactly once,
  // even if an

... [4047 more chars truncated]

</details>

### BUG: Inconsistent `REPLY` variable usage in `maestro_ask_yn`  
**Severity**: medium  
**Location**: `maestro_ask_yn`  
**Problem**: The `maestro_ask_yn` function sets the `REPLY` variable based on user input or a default. However, the subsequent checks for `REPLY` in the script (e.g., in `act1_hello_and_discovery`, `act2_install_prerequisites`, `uninstall`) often use `[ "$REPLY" = "y" ] || [ "$REPLY" = "Y" ] || [ "$REPLY" = "" ]` for a 'yes' response when the default is 'y', or `[ "$REPLY" = "y" ] || [ "$REPLY" = "Y" ]` when the default is 'n'. The `maestro_ask_yn` function itself already handles setting `REPLY` to the default if the user presses Enter. This makes the `|| [ "$REPLY" = "" ]` redundant and potentially confusing if the default is 'n'. More critically, if the default is 'y', and the user presses Enter, `REPLY` will be 'y', not empty. The current logic for checking `REPLY` is not consistently aligned with how `maestro_ask_yn` sets the default.  

**Fix**: Simplify the checks for `REPLY` after calling `maestro_ask_yn`. Since `maestro_ask_yn` already sets `REPLY` to the default if the user presses Enter, you only need to check for the normalized 'y' or 'n' value.  

For a 'yes' default:  
Change `if [ "$REPLY" != "y" ] && [ "$REPLY" != "Y" ] && [ "$REPLY" != "" ]; then` to `if [ "$REPLY" != "y" ]; then`  

For a 'no' default:  
Change `if [ "$REPLY" = "y" ] || [ "$REPLY" = "Y" ]; then` to `if [ "$REPLY" = "y" ]; then`  

This makes the logic clearer and less prone to errors.

**Location**: `handleBuild`  
**Intent**: The polling mechanism should consistently handle network failures or server errors during status checks.  
**Reality**: Inside the `setInterval` callback within `handleBuild`, there are two separate `try...catch` blocks. The outer `try...catch` handles the initial `fetch` call for `/api/plugin-builder/build`. The inner `try...catch` handles the `fetch` call for `/api/plugin-builder/builds/${data.buildId}`. However, the `catch` block for the inner `fetch` only increments `pollFailures.current` and checks if it's `>= 5` to clear the poll and set an error. The `if (!statusRes.ok)` branch, which indicates a server error response, also increments `pollFailures.current` and performs the same check. This duplication is not ideal and could be refactored for clarity and maintainability. More importantly, the `catch` block for the inner `fetch` does not distinguish between network errors and other potential runtime errors, treating them all as "Lost connection to build server".

The `path` should likely include `group.plugin` as well, or the `map` entries should be adjusted to reflect the actual location of skills within the marketplace's plugin structure. As it stands, the `path` and `map` combination will likely lead to the build script failing to find the marketplace skills.

### ISSUE: Ref state not reset on new scan

**Reality**: The `ref` state is initialized to 'main' but is not reset when a new URL is entered and scanned. If a user scans a repo with a specific branch, then changes the URL to a different repo without changing the branch input, the previous branch will be used for the new repo scan. ### ISSUE: Inconsistent `getSkillKey` usage for Marketplace skills  
**Severity**: medium  
**Location**: `SkillPicker` component, specifically within the `marketplace` tab rendering logic.  
**Intent**: The `getSkillKey` function is designed to generate a unique key for a skill selection, which is then used to check if a skill is already selected via `selectedKeys.has(key)`. For marketplace skills, `getSkillKey` uses `skill.id`.  
**Reality**: When rendering marketplace skills, the `key` variable is set to `marketplace:${skill.id}`. However, when adding a marketplace skill via `onAddSkill`, the `id` property of the `PluginSkillSelection` object is passed directly. This is consistent with `getSkillKey`. The issue is that the `key` prop for the `div` element is set to `skill.id` directly, not `marketplace:${skill.id}`. While React keys don't necessarily need to match the `selectedKeys` format, it's inconsistent and could lead to confusion or potential issues if `skill.id` alone isn't guaranteed to be unique across all skill types (though it should be unique within marketplace skills). More importantly, the `onRemoveSkill` call passes `key` (which is `marketplace:${skill.id}`), but the `onAddSkill` call passes an object where the `id` is just `skill.id`. This is fine because `getSkillKey` will correctly form the key from the `PluginSkillSelection` object. The primary inconsistency is the `key` prop of the `div` element.

---  

### ISSUE: Marketplace skill path construction  
**Severity**: high  
**Location**: generateManifest  
**Intent**: For marketplace skills, the `map` property in `PluginManifestSource` should correctly map the skill's path within the installed plugin directory to its desired path in the final plugin.  
**Reality**: In the `generateManifest` function, when processing marketplace skills, the `map` entry is constructed as `map[\`skills/${skillName}\`] = \`skills/${skillName}\` `. This assumes that the skill's actual path within the installed marketplace plugin is directly `skills/<skillName>`. However, the `installPath` is set to `path.join(os.homedir(), '.claude', 'plugins', 'marketplaces', group.marketplace, group.plugin)`. The skills within this installed plugin might not necessarily reside directly under a `skills/` directory at the root of `installPath`. The `PluginManifestSource` `map` property expects the key to be the source path relative to `path` and the value to be the destination path. The current implementation uses the same path for both, which is likely incorrect for marketplace skills unless all marketplace plugins strictly adhere to a `skills/<skillName>` structure at their root. This could lead to the plugin builder failing to find the actual skill files.  

### ISSUE: Repo skill path mapping  
**Severity**: high  
**Location**: generateManifest  
**Intent**: For repo skills, the `map` property in `PluginManifestSource` should correctly map the skill's path within the cloned repository to its desired path in the final plugin.  
**Reality**: In the `generateManifest` function, when processing repo skills, the `map` entry is constructed as `map[skill.skillPath] = \`skills/${skill.name}\` `. The `skill.skillPath` is the path to the skill's directory within   

... [986 more chars truncated]  

</details>

 * Plugin Builder Types

// ============================================================================  
// Build Configuration  
// ============================================================================  

/**  
 * Configuration for building a plugin  
 * Submitted by the UI to POST /api/plugin-builder/build  
 */  
export interface PluginBuildConfig {  
  name: string                         // Plugin name (e.g., "my-backend-agent")  
  version: string                      // Semver (e.g., "1.0.0")  
  description?: string                 // Human-readable description  
  skills: PluginSkillSelection[]       // Selected skills from various sources  
  includeHooks?: boolean               // Include default hooks (default: true)  
}  

/**  
 * A skill selected for inclusion in the plugin.  
 * Tagged union — the UI sends one of these per selected skill.  
 */  
export type PluginSkillSelection =  
  | { type: 'core'; name: string }  
  | { type: 'marketplace'; id: string; marketplace: string; plugin: string }  
  | { type: 'repo'; url: string; ref: string; skillPath: string; name: string }

// ============================================================================

  stats?: PluginBuildStats

}

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:32:29]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix a bug in: /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-a84928/components/plugin-builder/RepoScanner.tsx  

The `ref` state input has a controlled-value inconsistency. The `onChange` handler uses `setRef(e.target.value || 'main')` — when the user clears the input, the state becomes 'main' but the displayed value is an empty string (because `e.target.value` is empty), creating a visual inconsistency where UI doesn't match state.  

Fix:  
1. Change the ref input's `onChange` handler from `setRef(e.target.value || 'main')` to `setRef(e.target.value)` so the state always reflects what's displayed.  
2. In `handleScan`, where `ref` is used in the fetch request body, change `ref` to `ref || 'main'` so that an empty ref defaults to 'main' for the API call.  

This way the input is fully controlled (shows what the state is) and the default is applied only at the API call boundary.  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return to orchestrator ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] RepoScanner ref input - brief_result"  
- Max 2 lines back to orchestrator  

</div>

    21→**Severity**: high  
    22→**Location**: `act4_start_and_register`  
    23→**Problem**: When creating the `MAILMAN-CLAUDE.md` file for the mailman agent, the `portable_sed` command is used to substitute `{{ACTIVE_GATEWAYS_LIST}}`. The `gw_list` variable, which contains the formatted list of gateways, is passed directly to `portable_sed`. If `gw_list` contains characters that are special to `sed` (like `&`, `/`, `\`, `[`, `*`, etc.), `sed` will interpret them as part of the regular expression or replacement string, leading to incorrect substitutions or `sed` errors. This is especially problematic because `gw_list` is constructed with newlines (`\n`), which `sed` might misinterpret depending on the `sed` version and flags. The `safe_dir` variable is correctly escaped for `sed` metacharacters, but `gw_list` is not.

<summary><strong>Agent `a3dcdb28e946d3f7f` (unknown) [21 messages]</strong></summary>

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:25:47]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix a regression in: /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-a84928/scripts/remote-install.sh  

In `act4_start_and_register`, find the code that creates `safe_gw_list` (it was recently added). It currently looks like:  
```
safe_gw_list=$(printf '%s' "$gw_list" | sed 's/[[\.*^$|&\\\/]/\\&/g')
```

The problem: `gw_list` contains `\n` (literal backslash-n) for newlines in the bullet list. The escaping regex `s/[[\.*^$|&\\\/]/\\&/g` also escapes backslashes, so `\n` becomes `\\n`. When this is used in a sed replacement string with the `|` delimiter, `\\n` is treated as literal backslash-n, NOT as a newline — which means the MAILMAN-CLAUDE.md file would get literal `\n` characters instead of actual line breaks.  

The fix: Change the escaping to only escape characters that are special in sed replacement strings when using `|` as delimiter. Specifically: `&` (has special meaning in replacement) and `|` (the delimiter). Backslashes in `\n` sequences should NOT be escaped since sed interprets `\n` as a newline.  

Replace the safe_gw_list line with:  
```bash
safe_gw_list=$(printf '%s' "$gw_list" | sed 's/[&|]/\\&/g')
```

This correctly escapes `&` (sed replacement backreference) and `|` (the pipe delimiter used in portable_sed), without mangling the `\n` sequences that sed needs for newline insertion.  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return to orchestrator ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] remote-install.sh safe_gw_list - brief_result"  
- Max 2 lines back to orchestrator  

</div>

```typescript
const installPath = path.join(os.homedir(), '.claude', 'plugins', 'marketplaces', group.marketplace)
```

```typescript
const installPath = path.join(os.homedir(), '.claude', 'plugins', 'marketplaces', group.marketplace, group.plugin)
```

This ensures the build script looks for skills at `~/.claude/plugins/marketplaces/<marketplace>/<plugin>/skills/<skillName>` rather than `~/.claude/plugins/marketplaces/<marketplace>/skills/<skillName>`.

    20→### BUG: Incorrect `getSkillKey` for 'repo' type  
    21→**Severity**: high  
    22→**Location**: `getSkillKey`  
    23→**Problem**: The `getSkillKey` function for `repo` type skills uses `skill.url` and `skill.skillPath`. However, the `PluginSkillSelection` type for `repo` skills (as implied by `RepoScanner` and its `onAddSkill` prop) should include `repoId` and `skillId` to uniquely identify a skill within a scanned repository. Using `url` and `skillPath` might not be unique enough if multiple skills from the same path but different repos (or different versions of the same repo) are considered, or if the `skillPath` itself isn't unique across different skills within the same repo. More critically, the `RepoScanner` component's `onAddSkill` prop expects a `PluginSkillSelection` which, for `repo` type, should contain `repoId` and `skillId`. The current implementation of `getSkillKey` does not align with the expected structure of a `repo` skill as it would be added by `RepoScanner`.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:18:55]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have all the facts I need.  

Verified findings:  
1. The `PluginSkillSelection` type for `repo` uses `url` and `skillPath` (NOT `repoId`/`skillId`). The `getSkillKey` function is therefore correct — the LLM reviewer was wrong about this bug.  
2. Line 59: `useEffect` dependency array contains `[setMarketplaceSkills, setLoadingMarketplace]` — these are React `setState` functions which are stable references and must NOT be in the dependency array. This is a real bug: it causes the effect to declare false dependencies, which can trigger ESLint `exhaustive-deps` warnings and in pathological cases (if some future refactor replaces these with unstable references) would re-run the fetch loop. The correct deps array is `[]` since the effect is meant to run once on mount.  

Let me now apply the single fix needed.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:25:47]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix a single bug in: /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-a84928/components/plugin-builder/SkillPicker.tsx  

In the section rendering core skills (`activeTab === 'core'`), each skill is mapped with a `div`. Inside the map function, there is:  
  `const key = \`core:${skill.name}\``  
  `const isSelected = selectedKeys.has(key)`  
  ...  
  `<div key={skill.name} ...>`  

The `key` prop on the `<div>` should use the `key` variable (which is `core:${skill.name}`) instead of `skill.name`. Change:  
  `<div key={skill.name}`  
To:  
  `<div key={key}`  

This ensures React key consistency with the actual skill key format used throughout the component.

    20→### BUG: `clearPoll` dependency in `useEffect`  
    21→**Severity**: medium  
    22→**Location**: `BuildAction`  
    23→**Problem**: The `useEffect` hook for cleanup has `clearPoll` in its dependency array. While `clearPoll` is wrapped in `useCallback`, `useCallback` itself can return a new function instance if its dependencies change. In this specific case, `clearPoll` has no dependencies, so it will always be stable. However, if `clearPoll` were to ever have dependencies, listing it in `useEffect`'s dependency array could lead to the cleanup function being re-registered unnecessarily, or worse, if `clearPoll` itself was not properly memoized, it could lead to an infinite loop or unexpected behavior. The comment states "listing it in the dependency array keeps the linter and React happy and ensures the cleanup always uses the canonical clearPoll logic," which is a misunderstanding of `useEffect` dependencies. For cleanup functions, if the cleanup logic itself doesn't depend on props or state that ch

    20→### BUG: Incorrect query parameter parsing for `queryLongTermMemories`  
    21→**Severity**: medium  
    22→**Location**: `routes` array, handler for `GET /api/agents/([^/]+)/memory/long-term$`  
    23→**Problem**: The `queryLongTermMemories` function expects `query` and `memoryId` as distinct parameters. However, the current implementation passes `query.query || query.q` for the `query` parameter and `query.id` for the `memoryId` parameter. The `query` parameter in the service function is likely intended for the search string, while `memoryId` is for a specific memory ID. The current mapping `memoryId: query.id` is correct, but `query: query.query || query.q` might be problematic if the service expects `query` to be the actual search string and `query.query` or `query.q` are just aliases for it. More critically, the `query` parameter in the service function is typed as `string | undefined`, but it's being passed `query.query || query.q` which could be an empty string if both are undefined. This could lead to unexpected behavior in the service function if it expects `undefined`

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:19:57]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I understand the `queryLongTermMemories` function. At line 709: `if (view === 'context' && query)` and line 738: `if (query)` — both of these check `query` as a truthy value. An empty string `""` is falsy in JavaScript, so the behavior with `""` vs `undefined` is identical for these checks.  

However, the review suggests fixing `query.query || query.q` to add `|| undefined` to prevent passing an empty string. Let me look at the exact current code:  

Line 635: `query: query.query || query.q,`  

The `getQuery()` function returns parsed URL query parameters. If neither `query` nor `q` is present in the URL, `query.query` and `query.q` would be `undefined`, and `undefined || undefined = undefined`. So this won't produce an empty string — it only produces an empty string if the URL actually has `?query=` or `?q=` with an empty value. In that case, the service function handles it correctly because `if (query)` is falsy for `""`.  

The review's finding about this is a very marginal concern, not a real bug. The existing code is already correct.  

Now let me re-read the complete findings report to make sure I haven't missed the end of the last bug report.

`sendServiceResult` expects a plain object (reads `.status`, `.error`, `.data`). That confirms that if these functions were async (returning Promises), the bug would be real. But they are NOT async — they return plain `ServiceResult<T>` objects directly.

Now I have everything I need. The analysis is clear:  

1. `runBuild` is an `async function` that returns `Promise<void>` — it is fully awaitable.  
2. It sets the result status to either `'complete'` or `'failed'` before resolving.  
3. Currently `buildPlugin` fires it without `await`, so `activeOps` is decremented immediately after launch (not after completion), and the function returns `202` (Accepted) before the build finishes.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:19:05]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `plugin-builder-service.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-a84928/services/plugin-builder-service.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
    // Run build asynchronously; activeOps is decremented in the outer finally block
    // once the build is fully launched (or the launch itself fails).
    runBuild(buildId, buildDir, manifest).catch(err => {
      console.error(`Build ${buildId} failed:`, err)
      // Ensure status is updated even on unexpected errors
      const r = buildResults.get(buildId)
      if (r && r.status === 'building') {
        buildResults.set(buildId, {
          ...r,
          status: 'failed',
          logs: [err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err)],
        })
      }
    })

    return { data: result, status: 202 }
```

**New:**  
```
    // Await the full build so activeOps correctly limits concurrent complete build
    // operations (not just their launch). The finally block decrements activeOps
    // only after runBuild resolves or rejects.
    await runBuild(buildId, buildDir, manifest).catch(err => {
      console.error(`Build ${buildId} failed:`, err)
      // Ensure status is updated even on unexpected errors
      const r = buildResults.get(buildId)
      if (r && r.status === 'building') {
        buildResults.set(buildId, {
          ...r,
          status: 'failed',
          logs: [err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err)],
        })
      }
    })

    // Return the final build result now that the build has fully completed.
    const finalResult = buildResults.get(buildId)
    if (finalResult?.status === 'failed') {
      return { error: 'Plugin build failed', status: 500 }
    }
    return { data: finalResult || result, status: 200 }
```

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-a84928/services/plugin-builder-service.ts has been updated successfully.

   392→    // Return the final build result now that the build has fully completed.  
   393→    const finalResult = buildResults.get(buildId)  
   394→    if (finalResult?.status === 'failed') {  
   395→      return { error: 'Plugin build failed', status: 500 }  
   396→    }  
   397→    return { data: finalResult || result, status: 200 }  
   398→  } catch (error) {  
   399→    console.error('Error starting plugin build:', error)  
   400→    return { error: 'Failed to start plugin build', status: 500 }  
   401→  } finally {  
   402→    // Decrement exactly once, whether the try succeeded or threw.  
   403→    activeOps = Math.max(0, activeOps - 1)  
   404→  }  
   405→}  

[system reminder collapsed]  


</details>
